The key pattern is direct tracer initialization using `otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\")` with an empty instrumentation scope string.\\n\\n**Tracer Initialization:** Prometheus calls `otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\")` directly to obtain a tracer without specifying an instrumentation scope name (promql/engine.go:1919, scrape/scrape.go:748, storage/remote/client.go:290).\\n\\n**Span Start Pattern:** Spans are created with `ctx, span := otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\").Start(ctx, \\\"SpanName\\\", options)` where options can include `trace.WithSpanKind(trace.SpanKindClient)` for HTTP operations (e.g., scrape/scrape.go:748, storage/remote/client.go:290, storage/remote/client.go:402).\\n\\n**Span Attributes:** Uses `span.SetAttributes()` with individual attribute.String(), attribute.Int(), attribute.Float64() calls for setting span attributes (promql/engine.go:250, promql/engine.go:1922, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:2299-2310).\\n\\n**Span Events:** Uses `span.AddEvent(\\\"event_name\\\", trace.WithAttributes(...))` for logging events within spans (promql/engine.go:1101, promql/engine.go:1109).\\n\\n**Error Recording:** Uses `span.RecordError(err)` to record errors in spans without setting error status code manually (storage/remote/queue_manager.go:621, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1821, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1931).\\n\\n**Span Completion:** Always uses `defer span.End()` to ensure span completion (promql/engine.go:1920, scrape/scrape.go:749, storage/remote/client.go:291, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1807, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:601).\\n\\n**Helper Functions:** Prometheus defines `createBatchSpan()` in storage/remote/queue_manager.go (lines 2296-2313) as a helper function that encapsulates span creation and attribute setting for batch remote write operations.\\n\\n**HTTP Instrumentation:** Prometheus uses otelhttp and otelhttptrace packages for automatic HTTP span instrumentation. The scrape package uses `otelhttp.NewTransport()` and `otelhttptrace.NewClientTrace()` for HTTP client tracing (scrape/scrape.go:2265-2268, storage/remote/client.go:161, storage/remote/client.go:223-226).\\n\\n## Grafana Patterns:\\n\\nGrafana uses OpenTelemetry with a more structured approach through dependency injection. The tracer provider is initialized globally and tracers are obtained with specific instrumentation scope names.\\n\\n**Tracer Provider Setup:** In pkg/infra/tracing/tracing.go, the `ProvideService()` function (lines 83-106) initializes a TracingService that sets up the global tracer provider via `otel.SetTracerProvider(tp)` (tracing.go:110, tracing.go:278). The TracingService supports multiple exporter types including Jaeger (initJaegerTracerProvider), OTLP (otlptracegrpc), and noop.\\n\\n**Global Tracer Function:** In pkg/server/wire.go (lines 215-217), the `otelTracer()` function serves as a wire provider that returns a tracer with the \\\"grafana\\\" instrumentation scope: `otel.GetTracerProvider().Tracer(\\\"grafana\\\")`.\\n\\n**Module-Specific Tracers:** Different Grafana modules declare their own package-level tracers with specific instrumentation scopes. Examples include: `tracer := otel.GetTracerProvider().Tracer(\\\"github.com/grafana/grafana/pkg/api\\\")` (pkg/api/api.go), dashboard service (pkg/services/dashboards/service/dashboard_service.go), access control (pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/accesscontrol.go), and zanzana client (pkg/services/authz/zanzana/client/client.go).\\n\\n**Span Start Pattern:** Most Grafana code uses `ctx, span := tracer.Start(ctx, \\\"span.name\\\")` with the pre-obtained tracer variable. The context parameter is often `c.Req.Context()` for HTTP handlers or a passed context (pkg/api/dashboard.go:50, pkg/api/dashboard.go:87, apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go:234).\\n\\n**Helper Function for Spans with Attributes:** The dashboard migration package defines `TracingStart()` in apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/tracing_helper.go (lines 15-17) as a helper that wraps span creation and directly applies attributes. This uses the pattern: `trace.SpanFromContext(ctx).TracerProvider().Tracer(instrumentationScope).Start(ctx, name, trace.WithAttributes(attributes...))`. This approach creates spans only if an existing span context is already in the current context.\\n\\n**Span Attributes:** Grafana uses `span.SetAttributes()` with multiple attributes passed as variadic arguments. For example, in apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go (lines 244-246): `span.SetAttributes(attribute.String(\\\"dashboard.uid\\\", info.uid)); span.SetAttributes(attribute.Int(\\\"source.schema_version\\\", int(schemaVer)))`. Span attributes in conversion and reconciliation operations are also set through the helper function's arguments (apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/zanzana_service.go uses SetAttributes for tuple counts and other metrics).\\n\\n**Error Recording:** Uses `span.RecordError(err)` for recording errors (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go:265, apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/folder_reconciler.go, apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/zanzana_service.go). In some cases, errors are also recorded by calling `span.SetStatus(codes.Error, ...)` after RecordError.\\n\\n**Span Completion:** Always uses `defer span.End()` to ensure spans are properly closed (pkg/api/dashboard.go:51, pkg/api/dashboard.go:88, apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go).\\n\\n**Middleware Integration:** Grafana integrates OpenTelemetry tracing at multiple middleware levels:\\n- HTTP request tracing in pkg/middleware/request_tracing.go\\n- gRPC tracing in pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/tracing.go\\n- HTTP client tracing in pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/tracing_middleware.go\\n\\n## Key Differences:\\n\\n1. **Scope Definition**: Prometheus uses empty string scope names (`\\\"\\\"`), while Grafana uses descriptive scope names like \\\"grafana\\\" or full package paths.\\n2. **Tracer Acquisition**: Prometheus acquires tracers on-demand inline, while Grafana pre-obtains tracers at package or module initialization.\\n3. **Context Handling**: Prometheus passes contexts through function calls, while Grafana often extracts context from HTTP requests using `c.Req.Context()`.\\n4. **Helper Functions**: Prometheus provides minimal helpers (createBatchSpan), while Grafana provides TracingStart that conditionally creates spans based on existing context.\\n5. **HTTP Instrumentation**: Prometheus explicitly uses otelhttp and otelhttptrace, while Grafana integrates tracing through middleware interfaces.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

repositories.\\n\\n## Prometheus Patterns:\\n\\nPrometheus uses OpenTelemetry for query execution and remote storage operations. The key pattern is direct tracer initialization using `otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\")` with an empty instrumentation scope string.\\n\\n**Tracer Initialization:** Prometheus calls `otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\")` directly to obtain a tracer without specifying an instrumentation scope name (promql/engine.go:1919, scrape/scrape.go:748, storage/remote/client.go:290).\\n\\n**Span Start Pattern:** Spans are created with `ctx, span := otel.Tracer(\\\"\\\").Start(ctx, \\\"SpanName\\\", options)` where options can include `trace.WithSpanKind(trace.SpanKindClient)` for HTTP operations (e.g., scrape/scrape.go:748, storage/remote/client.go:290, storage/remote/client.go:402).\\n\\n**Span Attributes:** Uses `span.SetAttributes()` with individual attribute.String(), attribute.Int(), attribute.Float64() calls for setting span attributes (promql/engine.go:250, promql/engine.go:1922, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:2299-2310).\\n\\n**Span Events:** Uses `span.AddEvent(\\\"event_name\\\", trace.WithAttributes(...))` for logging events within spans (promql/engine.go:1101, promql/engine.go:1109).\\n\\n**Error Recording:** Uses `span.RecordError(err)` to record errors in spans without setting error status code manually (storage/remote/queue_manager.go:621, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1821, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1931).\\n\\n**Span Completion:** Always uses `defer span.End()` to ensure span completion (promql/engine.go:1920, scrape/scrape.go:749, storage/remote/client.go:291, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1807, storage/remote/queue_manager.go:601).\\n\\n**Helper Functions:** Prometheus defines `createBatchSpan()` in storage/remote/queue_manager.go (lines 2296-2313) as a helper function that encapsulates span creation and attribute setting for batch remote write operations.\\n\\n**HTTP Instrumentation:** Prometheus uses otelhttp and otelhttptrace packages for automatic HTTP span instrumentation. The scrape package uses `otelhttp.NewTransport()` and `otelhttptrace.NewClientTrace()` for HTTP client tracing (scrape/scrape.go:2265-2268, storage/remote/client.go:161, storage/remote/client.go:223-226).\\n\\n## Grafana Patterns:\\n\\nGrafana uses OpenTelemetry with a more structured approach through dependency injection. The tracer provider is initialized globally and tracers are obtained with specific instrumentation scope names.\\n\\n**Tracer Provider Setup:** In pkg/infra/tracing/tracing.go, the `ProvideService()` function (lines 83-106) initializes a TracingService that sets up the global tracer provider via `otel.SetTracerProvider(tp)` (tracing.go:110, tracing.go:278). The TracingService supports multiple exporter types including Jaeger (initJaegerTracerProvider), OTLP (otlptracegrpc), and noop.\\n\\n**Global Tracer Function:** In pkg/server/wire.go (lines 215-217), the `otelTracer()` function serves as a wire provider that returns a tracer with the \\\"grafana\\\" instrumentation scope: `otel.GetTracerProvider().Tracer(\\\"grafana\\\")`.\\n\\n**Module-Specific Tracers:** Different Grafana modules declare their own package-level tracers with specific instrumentation scopes. Examples include: `tracer := otel.GetTracerProvider().Tracer(\\\"github.com/grafana/grafana/pkg/api\\\")` (pkg/api/api.go), dashboard service (pkg/services/dashboards/service/dashboard_service.go), access control (pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/accesscontrol.go), and zanzana client (pkg/services/authz/zanzana/client/client.go).\\n\\n**Span Start Pattern:** Most Grafana code uses `ctx, span := tracer.Start(ctx, \\\"span.name\\\")` with the pre-obtained tracer variable. The context parameter is often `c.Req.Context()` for HTTP handlers or a passed context (pkg/api/dashboard.go:50, pkg/api/dashboard.go:87, apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go:234).\\n\\n**Helper Function for Spans with Attributes:** The dashboard migration package defines `TracingStart()` in apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/tracing_helper.go (lines 15-17) as a helper that wraps span creation and directly applies attributes. This uses the pattern: `trace.SpanFromContext(ctx).TracerProvider().Tracer(instrumentationScope).Start(ctx, name, trace.WithAttributes(attributes...))`. This approach creates spans only if an existing span context is already in the current context.\\n\\n**Span Attributes:** Grafana uses `span.SetAttributes()` with multiple attributes passed as variadic arguments. For example, in apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go (lines 244-246): `span.SetAttributes(attribute.String(\\\"dashboard.uid\\\", info.uid)); span.SetAttributes(attribute.Int(\\\"source.schema_version\\\", int(schemaVer)))`. Span attributes in conversion and reconciliation operations are also set through the helper function's arguments (apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/zanzana_service.go uses SetAttributes for tuple counts and other metrics).\\n\\n**Error Recording:** Uses `span.RecordError(err)` for recording errors (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go:265, apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/folder_reconciler.go, apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/zanzana_service.go). In some cases, errors are also recorded by calling `span.SetStatus(codes.Error, ...)` after RecordError.\\n\\n**Span Completion:** Always uses `defer span.End()` to ensure spans are properly closed (pkg/api/dashboard.go:51, pkg/api/dashboard.go:88, apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/metrics.go).\\n\\n**Middleware Integration:** Grafana integrates OpenTelemetry tracing at multiple middleware levels:\\n- HTTP request tracing in pkg/middleware/request_tracing.go\\n- gRPC tracing in pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/tracing.go\\n- HTTP client tracing in pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/tracing_middleware.go\\n\\n## Key Differences:\\n\\n1. **Scope Definition**: Prometheus uses empty string scope names (`\\\"\\\"`), while Grafana uses descriptive scope names like \\\"grafana\\\" or full package paths.\\n2. **Tracer Acquisition**: Prometheus acquires tracers on-demand inline, while Grafana pre-obtains tracers at package or module initialization.\\n3. **Context Handling**: Prometheus passes contexts through function calls, while Grafana often extracts context from HTTP requests using `c.Req.Context()`.\\n4. **Helper Functions**: Prometheus provides minimal helpers (createBatchSpan), while Grafana provides TracingStart that conditionally creates spans based on existing context.\\n5. **HTTP Instrumentation**: Prometheus explicitly uses otelhttp and otelhttptrace, while Grafana integrates tracing through middleware interfaces.\"\n}\n","numLines":47,"startLine":1,"totalLines":47}}}
